EPILOGUE
Since then, Oprah and I have become friends, having watched each other cautiously from a distance. But it was a fascinating moment for me. Rap, as I said at the beginning of the book, is basically an art form that gave voice to a specific experience, but, like all art, it is ultimately about the most common human experiences: joy, pain, fear, desire, uncertainty. , hope, anger, love - crew love, family love, even romantic love (put on "The Miseducation of Lauryn Hill" sometime and tell me that rap can't be romantic - or if you want to keep it on the street, put on Mary J. Blige and Method Man's "I'll be there for you / You are all I need to survive"). Of course, in the end, it may not be the art form for you. Oprah, for example, still can't get over the n-word problem (or the black problem, with all apologies to Mrs. Winfrey). I can respect your position. For her, it is about recognizing the deep and painful history of the word. For me, it is just a word, a word whose power is owned by the user and his intention. People empower words, so banning a word is useless, really. "Nigga" becomes "mono porch" becomes "coon" and so on if that is what is in a person's heart. The key is to change the person. And we change people through conversation, not through censorship. This is why I want people to understand what the words we use, and the stories we tell, are really about.
But great MCing isn't just about filling the song meter with rhythm and melody. The other ways that poets make words work is by giving them layers of meaning, so you can use them to get to complicated truths in a way that direct narration cannot. The word he uses can be read in a dozen different ways: they can be fun and serious. They can be symbolic and literal. They can be clearly obvious and subliminally effective at the same time. The art of rap is misleading. It seems so direct, personal and real that people read it completely literally, like raw testimony or autobiography. And sometimes the words we use, nigga, bitch, motherfucker, and the violence of the images overwhelms some listeners, it's all white noise for them until they hear a bitch or a nigga and then they run screaming "Look ! " and they feel vindicated in their limited conception of what music is about. But that would be like listening to Maya Angelou and ignoring everything until you hear her talk about drinking or sleeping with someone's husband and then fire her as an alcoholic adulteress.
In places like Marcy, there are people who know the ins and outs of government bureaucracies, police procedures, and sentencing guidelines, who spend half their lives in dirty waiting rooms in plastic chairs waiting for someone to call them by name. But despite all this involvement, the government could very well be the weather because many of us don't think we have anything to do with it; We do not believe that we have any control over what controls us. Many of our heroes, almost by default, were people who tried to dismantle or overthrow the government, Malcolm X or Black Panthers, or people who tried to make it completely irrelevant, like Marcus Garvey, who wanted blacks to sail. Back to Africa. The government was everywhere, and we hate it.

We are 10,000 feet above Compton in a private jet, and Kendrick Lamar explains to me what happened to him yesterday when he disappeared. We had a plan: Kendrick was going to give me a guided tour, guided by the G-funk-star synthesizer in his neighborhood, where he still lives more or less, starting at his parents' house a couple of blocks from his old school High School, Centennial High, near the corner of Piru and South Central. Instead, AWOL left. All day, no one from his label, Interscope, or Top Dawg Entertainment, the baby Death Row Records who originally signed him, could locate him. Kendrick was gone.
I asked him if this meant things were okay between him and Drake. The pause. "Very cool." Shrugs "And I mean, it would be nice if we weren't."
A month later, it became apparent that things between Kendrick and Drake were definitely not great. After Drake's new album was released, he gave a couple of interviews in which he sounded hurt by the "Control" thing: "You can't say that and then see me and say, 'Yeah, man, what's up?' - pretending nothing ever happened. " Apparently in response, during the encryption of the BET Hip-Hop Awards, a few weeks later, Kendrick went free-style: nothing has been the same since they left "Control" / and tucked a sensitive rapper into their clothing. Pijama.
When Kendrick Lamar was 21, 2Pac appeared to him in a vision. Before rolling his eyes, Lamar wants you to know that he is not the hermit type, on the edge of the Nitrio Desert, who sees the vision. He knows what this sounds like.
Much of Kendrick's music now is an attempt to transcend his devastated world without parting with him at trial, about somehow gaining control over the chaos in his home: some of his uncles were Crips, and his father allegedly He was a Gangster Disciple in Chicago before moving to Chicago. Compton, and for her neighborhood's distorted commitment to teen pride. It is an ethos that extends to your crew. They have a seriousness of purpose, a rigorous discipline that can sometimes seem a bit monastic. Kendrick does not smoke weed or drink alcohol. In my time with him, I never saw anyone roll even a jay's thinnest spider leg, nor did I see Kendrick as much as looking at the many, many girls around him. "When I ask OGs why there is so much division in the streets, nobody really knows," he says. "But do you know one thing everyone always mentions? A woman."
